This was a crepe place many years ago, had some of the best seafood crepes. Now the menu has changed quite a bit,  its somewhere between a bistro and a diner. The wait can be a bit to get in as the place is really small,  but once in service is quick and courteous.  Food is tasty, reasonably priced and the portions are good sized. Wife had the French onion soup, I the omelette,  both very good.  Brianna the server was very pleasant.</text>

This is the perfect place to eat during a shopping trip - the food is tasty, the portions are reasonable but not too large, and the service is great. I got a sandwich combo with french onion soup, and the sandwich was on a delightfully small croissant. (It was the perfect size to let me go shopping for pants later.) < review>
A completely amazing experience! I'm not sure where to even begin, but I wish I could give them 15 stars for customer service and the overall experience.
- Ease of renting. 5⭐ 's. We decided late Saturday night to rent a Harley on Sunday. After looking at all the options to rent through different agencies we choose HDSD (EagleRider SD) because of the varieties of bikes, you're guaranteed the quality and assurance of riding a top notch HD motorcycle, plus all the equipment is included.
- In store experience 5+5⭐'s.  I wish I could name everyone in this store because they're all awesome! Down to earth, happy, helpful, bike loving people.  Brandon and Ryan are the reason we had such a great day.  Brandon handled the rental, did the service check, walked me through the bike from wheel to wheel, broke out a map and we talked through the route and what would enhance the ride, and got us out the door. He also checked us back in and we talked about the different styles HD is carrying as a comparison for what we rode   Ryan walked with us around the shop, pulled up maps on his phone, and made some suggestions to the route to make sure we had the most scenic ride possible.  No way we would have seen what we did on our trip without him.
- The bike. 5 ⭐'s.  We rented a Street Glide Grand Touring bike. It really doesn't get much better.  It handled like a luxury performance vehicle, no surprise it's Harley Davidson! We took the scenic route up to Julian and back.  Lots of curves, fast highway straight aways, and the ever present cross winds in the valley and we cruised right through them all with a smile. Lots of storage space, comfortable seats, my better half was in heaven on the back seat.
- Overall 5+5+5⭐'s.  No clue why we haven't done this sooner.  It's great to have the option to try out different motorcycles and away for a day or a weekend in a completely different way then driving or flying somewhere and there's nothing like the experience.  We WILL be coming back and when it's time to finally decided on a bike to call our own, you can guarantee it'll be from the EagleRider San Diego family< /review>

Brandon and Ryan are the reason we had such a great day.  Brandon handled the rental, did the service check, walked me through the bike from wheel to wheel, broke out a map and we talked through the route and what would enhance the ride, and got us out the door. He also checked us back in and we talked about the different styles HD is carrying as a comparison for what we rode   Ryan walked with us around the shop, pulled up maps on his phone, and made some suggestions to the route to make sure we had the most scenic ride possible.  No way we would have seen what we did on our trip without him.
- The bike. 5 ⭐'s.  We rented a Street Glide Grand Touring bike. It really doesn't get much better.  It handled like a luxury performance vehicle, no surprise it's Harley Davidson! We took the scenic route up to Julian and back.  Lots of curves, fast highway straight aways, and the ever present cross winds in the valley and we cruised right through them all with a smile. Lots of storage space, comfortable seats, my better half was in heaven on the back seat.
- Overall 5+5+5⭐'s.  No clue why we haven't done this sooner.  It's great to have the option to try out different motorcycles and away for a day or a weekend in a completely different way then driving or flying somewhere and there's nothing like the experience.  We WILL be coming back and when it's time to finally decided on a bike to call our own, you can guarantee it'll be from the EagleRider San Diego family< /text><name>Matt Curran<//name>< Rating>

<Name>Hiya Myatt< /Name><Date>1592068195019</Date><rating>4<//rating><Review>This store has really cute stationery and K-Pop goods. There are may pros and a few cons to the place. First, the K-Pop goods are usually high quality with a great selection. You should expect many BTS, NCT, WANNA ONE, EXO, Red Velvet, TWICE, and BLACKPINK products. But don't worry, sometimes, theres other groups' merchandise in stock, like SHINee, SEVENTEEN, WINNER, and Super Junior. They sell lots of K-Pop albums too. But, a majority of the albums are from more popular groups and artists and are newer releases. I've seen plenty of K-Pop posters, sweaters, socks, notebooks, calendars, note cards, photocards, pencil cases, bags, backpacks, pillows, and pens. A majority of the K-Pop merchandise is unofficial and are sent in from other K-Pop stores over in South Korea. This takes me to a con, the stuff there can be REALLY overpriced. A K-Pop album that can  only cost $13 on amazon.com can cost around $37 at K-Pop Fancy. I can only imagine someone buying albums from K-Pop Fancy if they're impatient, in a hurry, or don't want to buy from amazon.com.

Besides all the K-Pop stuff they sell, K-Pop Fancy also sells Anime merchandise from Sailor Moon and Dragonball Z. I believe that most of the merchandise are figures and keychains. They also sell Studio Ghibli products, most of which are unofficial. But, they sell Totoro plushies and stationery. They sell an assortment of high quality Korean stationery. You can expect a single pen to cost $2 to $3. They have a stock of Kakao Friends and cute character notebooks for about $5. They also have a whole shelving unit of pencil cases that range from $6 to $19.

Another thing they sell are squishies. They're all super cute but also super expensive. A medium sized squishy costs about $17. Lastly, they sell accessories like hair clips and earrings. There's a very little assortment of earrings, but they are cute. K-Pop Fancy is a great place to quickly get some K-Pop merchandise or stationery. But, if you're not in a hurry, save yourself some money and buy the stuff on amazon.com or something like that. It's currently the only K-Pop store in San Diego County, so, I highly recommend visiting this cute little shop for some cute little things!

8/14/18 Edit:

The other day, I walked into K-pop Fancy with the rest of my family. Overwhelmed with the K-pop idols, cramped space, and the music inside, both of my parents walked out of the store and stood next to the entrance, waiting for me to make my purchase. Not even one minute after they left, the cashier/employee almost rudely told me that I couldn't be in there without a parent. (Mind you that I'm in highschool) Frustrated, I left the store to bring one of my parents back in the store. I could tell both of my parents also shared my frustration. I made my purchase, and the cashier was quite frustrated with me like I didn't buy enough stuff or that she's still mad that I was in the store without a parent for less than a minute.

I only go in there these days to look at albums and buy maybe 1 pen. It's no fun to have employees scowling at you and starting at every movement you make all the time. K-pop albums are still way too overpriced. SF9's Sensuous album was $36 last time I was there and it's only $28 on Amazon. SHINee's The Story of Light Ep.3 album was $37 at K-Pop Fancy and they're being sold on Amazon for less than $21. I actually feel bad for the people who buy albums at K-pop Fancy. With all the money that they would've saved buying albums on Amazon, they could've bought a couple more albums on Amazon!

Overall, I really wouldn't recommend this place to anyone, unless they want expensive non-official K-pop  or anime merch. Maybe I'll go back when there is a new person enjoyed there. But for now, I will not patronize a business with rude employees and expensive prices.

6/13/20 Edit:

I recently went there to pict up The Misconceptions of Us by SHINee and Neo Zone by NCT 127. Their prices are much cheaper now and sometimes even cheaper than Amazon/eBay! Sadly, my SHINee album was very, very damaged.< /Review>< Pictures>

<rate>4</rate><Text>I liked this store, all the K-Pop and anime merchandise was amazing. 10/5/17 Edit:  I have visited a few more times, there are now more helpful, kinder staff.  Though the K-Pop albums can be up to $30 more than the prices on Amazon, the prices are kind-of reasonable.  I believe that the stock is mostly shipped from South Korea, so please keep that in mind when being overwhelmed with the prices.  I wish there was more Seventeen merch there, but BTS is my bias group so I'm "fine".  What I do like in the little shop is that you can see the physical K-Pop albums and actually look and hold them instead of looking at digital photos of K-Pop albums on Amazon.  That doesn't mean I'd buy the albums there, I recommend buying on Amazon still.  Also, there are many (sort of) smaller K-Pop groups' albums there like NCT Dream, Red Velvet, and f(x) just to name a few.  They also sell K-Pop socks from BTS, BIGBANG, TWICE, GOT7, EXO, and some other groups.  Sadly, this is one of the only K-Pop stores in the area, so it can be quite a drive for some K-Pop fans.  The music in the market (Not Kpop Fancy)  is great!  I've heard I Luv It (PSY) and Fire (BTS) on the speaker!   The food around Kpop Fancy is great too, you should try it.  Overall, I recommend visiting, though it can be a hit or miss for some people.  I personally love it, I go there every other week.< /Text>< Pics>

<name>Mike Hua<//name><time>1526452020243</time>< Rating>
2<//Rating>
< review>
I was in town looking for a Chinese lunch spot. Upon arrival, the wait was conspicuously long, but decided to wait because the soup dumplings looked really appetizing. When getting seated after 30 minutes, I realized that the restaurant was severely understaffed not only outside the kitchen but also inside as well for a Sunday noon service. Long story short, we put order in for 4 dishes but only ate 2 because they simply couldn't turn around the remaining 2 dishes within 20 minutes of serving the first two. The waiter was nice enough to explain the under-staffing situation, but assessing the situation at the time, we suspected even another 20 minutes wouldn't be enough.

On to the review of the dishes. The soup dumplings were actually not bad. I could tell they were freshly made and the dough skins were made very thin and chewy, just the way I like them. The fillings were fairly soupy and the soup was light and flavorful, but not too oily. Although they executed this dish very well, I was heavily disappointed in the other two dishes. The smoke fish was one of the worst I've had because it was clear to me that the dish was made a while ago - too cold even for a cold dish - and the execution was rather poor. The fish tasted extremely bland even when I smothered them in sauce. I always enjoyed eating this dish growing up because the father-side of my family always prepared this dish. It really bothered me that they completely butchered this dish. Finally, the soy milk with Chinese You-Tiao is at best mediocre because they've managed over-soak the You-Tiao to the point it was falling apart. All in all, if I were to return again, probably will just stick to the safe dishes like the soup dumplings.< /review>

<UserId.>115014077999082450395</UserId.>< username>
Cecilia Knapp< /username>
< date>
1577685477801</date>
<rate>3<//rate>< Review>
It's just ok, I've definitely had better dumplings at other places. My friend, who is vegetarian, brought me, my brother, and nephew here to try. She said her non-vegetarian friend really liked it and she at least has some options. We had an order of the pork XLB, pork pan-fried dumplings, green onion pancake, vegetarian potstickers, and stir-fried rice cakes. These are all items I've had at other places and I was underwhelmed. The wrapper on the XLB were too thick, though our order did come out nice and hot. There was a good amount of broth and the taste of the pork was good, the wrapper was just way too thick and doughy. Same with the pan-fried dumplings - they were almost as thick and doughy as steamed pork buns that you'd get a dim sum, but with the little pork meatball inside. The green onion pancakes were fried nice and golden and had a good taste, they just weren't flakey layers like I'm used to, but at least they were not oily. I didn't try the vegetarian potstickers but they did erroneously give us pork ones at first which my vegetarian friend found out after she bit into one. The rice cakes were ok, nothing extra special about them.

It was easy to find street parking and walk right in to get a table for 4 at 6:30 on a Sunday, but I don't know that I'm ever planning to go back.</Review>

< text>
This is based on my experience of their soup dumplings only. These are supposed to be filled with a good spoonful of hot soup when you bite into it, hence the name. Thus, when I order some, I'm not hoping to just get lucky that one of my dumplings will come with soup inside.

None of the pork and crab soup dumplings had any soup inside...when they arrived, it was clear they rushed the wrapping and everything had spilled inside the bamboo steamer. It's really a shame...it wasn't that busy when we went either. Regular pork dumplings were juicy, but also same problem. It's just not soup dumplings.

Cleanliness and decor is about the same as you would expect in any hole in the wall restaurant. Service was adequate, but food was subpar. Maybe their other dishes are better, but if your shop's name is Shanghai Dumpling shop then you should really be excellent at your namesake.<//text>

<Rate>4</Rate><review>Authentic Chinese food. Yummy dumplings!

Came by on a Sunday evening for dinner. There was a line outside the restaurant, we waited for approx 15mins before we were seated.

We were promptly served with tea and shortly after, a server came by to take our orders. We ordered Hot and Sour soup (3/5), Shanghai Dumplings (4/5), buns with condensed milk (4/5) and Beef with capsicum (3/5).

I had wanted to order their savory soy bean milk, unfortunately they are only available for breakfast/lunch.

The portions were huge for each of the dishes, enough for 3-4 to share. It was two of us so we ended up packing quite a bit of food home.

Overall, the food are authentic and tasty. Typical Chinese restaurants are really noisy, this was manageable.

Will be back again.<//review>< Pics>

< Text>
I went here on our search for shanghai Dumplings.  I've got to say, that these were some of the best that I've had in the Bay Area.  They had a tasty flavor and there was actually soup in most of the dumplings.

As for the restaurant itself, it is not a flashy store front located right on Broadway in Millbrae.  We were asked to put our name on a list when we arrived even though there was a large number of open tables.  We were seated quite quickly, but the service was somewhat rushed and when we tried to get our waiters attention for either a glass of cold water or our bill, it was quite tough to gain his attention.

Would I go back despite the service, sure!< /Text>

Arun Venkatesan</name>
<Time>1386377086403<//Time><rate>4</rate>< Text>
If you come here on the weekend or any other peak time, be ready to wait. We waited for 40 minutes for Sunday lunch.

The food here is definitely better than the average dumpling place. We had the soup dumplings (xiao long bao) and a few other varieties. The service was great. The owners and waiters treated us like children.

The decor and atmosphere is standard for true Chinese restaurants like this. Expect some hustle and bustle along with laughing, children playing, etc. Definitely the kind of place that could make you feel alive.

Come here with friends or family. You won't be disappointed.<//Text>

I went with 3 other people around 1pm on a Sunday and waited almost 1/2 an hour to get a table, with 5 people ahead of me when we signed up. We quickly ordered and the food came out quickly. Would I come back? Only if I'm in the neighborhood...< /Text>

<time>1345507440743</time><rate>5</rate><pictures>None<//pictures>< Review>
Outstanding food and service.

We stumbled across this shop on a family trip, staying in Millbrae the night before a flight from SFO.  Went in because we were hungry and no one could agree on anything else.  Once in, other diners enthusiastically told us we had made the right choose (and gave menu suggestions).  Our waiter appeared to be the manager as well, and was very patient with a bunch of American bumpkins.  Food was outstanding, and portions were very generous.  Can't recall the prices, but they were very reasonable.

Not sure when we will next be in Millbrae, but would certainly eat here again (and am telling all of my Bay Area friends).< /Review>

Mike Shaheen<//Name>
< Date>
1478719406574</Date>
< Rating>
5<//Rating>
< Text>
As a newcomer 3 years ago to "real" Chinese food (you other midwest transplants probably know what I'm talking about) I made it my quest to try xiao long bao (the steamed dumplings with pork & soup) at every Shanghainese restaurant that offered it.

My wife's is Cantonese and grew up in the bay area with a restaraunt loving family, so over the years I have collected a list of dumpling rating criteria.

The ratios are arguably the most important criteria  to me.  If there is too little soup, there is less flavor.  If the dumpling is too thick, it can mask the flavor.  If there is not enough pork...well you see where I'm going with this.

Other xiao long bao issues:
- Served in a tiny foil tin that almost invariably sticks to dumpling
- Very salty broth
- Tough and/or dense port

This is turning into a food theory post, so I'll get to the point.

The Shanghai Dumpling Shop consistently serves delicious Xiao Long Bao.  I know the ratios preference is matter of opinion and maybe you like really salty soup, but I think these are the BEST.

And, maybe the highest praise I can offer in our hyper-critical Bay Area dining market:  "I have never heard anyone say anything bad about these wonderful dumplings."<//Text>

< Name>
Nei Ng</Name>
< Review>
I had dinner here with a few friends, and it wasn't bad. After a brief wait, we were seated inside, and our waitress was surprisingly nice. She was more warm and welcoming than what you'd expect from typical Chinese service. Our food came pretty fast, too. Yay.

Stir Fried Pea Sprouts with Garlic - I liked the strong garlic flavor, but some of the pea sprouts were stiff around the stalks. The flavor wasn't bad, but the quality could've been better.

Stir Fried Rice Cakes - Mushy. Some pieces kept sticking to my teeth, which was annoying. They tasted pretty savory, but some more wok hei would've been better. I should mention that I'm not a super big fan of rice cakes, so I'm a little biased here.

Shanghai Stir Fried Noodles - Pretty good. The noodles had a tender, smooth bite that I liked. They had a savory flavor like the rice cakes but with a more enjoyable texture.

XLB - The skins were thin and broke open smoothly. There was a healthy amount of broth inside, and it had a very slight bitterness that reminded me of ginseng. Although I liked that part, I still thought it could've been more aromatic. More ginger and green onions would've made the flavors pop out more. The texture of the pork stuffing was a little on the gritty side, too. Still, the XLB weren't bad, but I wouldn't go out of my way to come here.<//Review>

< rating>
4</rating>
< review>
Recommend this place. You can find many traditional and common Chinese entrees here, including homestyle entrees and Chinese street food, e.g., sweet soy milk and Chinese donut. They also make great Chinese donuts and crab meat xiao long bao. Their food is authentic Chinese and overall well-made and delicious. However, as with many casual Chinese restaurants, there isn't much in terms of food presentation. The service is fast and friendly. In terms of decor and ambiance, this is not a hole-in the-wall joint, but the place needs updated chairs and renovation. Because of the delicious food, this place can get crowded, lending to a lively atmosphere. Overall a great and enjoyable eating experience lending a little bit of nostalgia for those of us who enjoyed Chinese street food growing up.< /review>
